Task instruction sent to agent 
# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# big-code-k8s-arch-001: Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture

## Task

Explain the Kubernetes scheduler architecture and how a Pod gets assigned to a Node. Trace the complete scheduling pipeline from when a Pod enters the scheduling queue to when it is bound to a Node, including the plugin framework, extension points, and the two-phase (scheduling cycle + binding cycle) design.

## Context

- **Repository**: kubernetes/kubernetes (Go, ~2.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: pkg/scheduler/ — the kube-scheduler component

## Requirements

1. Identify all files involved in the scheduler subsystem (scheduler core, framework, queue, cache, plugins)
2. Trace the dependency chain from the main scheduling loop through the scheduling cycle and binding cycle
3. Document the plugin framework architecture (extension points: PreFilter, Filter, Score, Reserve, Permit, Bind)
4. Explain how the SchedulingQueue, Cache, and CycleState interact during a scheduling cycle

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

64-assistanttext-
I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes scheduler architecture. Here's what I found:

## Summary

The Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated **two-phase plugin framework architecture**:

### Phase 1: Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous)
- Finds a suitable node for the pod using a series of **14 extension points**
- Uses plugins for filtering (feasibility) and scoring (ranking)
- Parallelizes Filter and Score plugins across nodes for performance
- Uses snapshot isolation to avoid race conditions during async binding
- Ends by "assuming" the pod in the cache before binding completes

### Phase 2: Binding Cycle (Asynchronous)  
- Persists the pod-to-node binding to the API server
- Runs asynchronously so scheduler doesn't block on API responses
- If binding fails, cleanup is triggered to revert the assumed state

### Key Design Patterns
1. **Two-Phase Design** — Separate find (sync) and bind (async) for high throughput
2. **Assume Pattern** — Optimistically update cache before binding succeeds
3. **Plugin Framework** — Complete scheduling logic is customizable via plugins at 14 strategic extension points
4. **Snapshot Isolation** — Work with immutable cluster snapshots to avoid conflicts
5. **Parallelization** — Filter/Score plugins run in parallel across nodes
6. **Three-Queue Model** — activeQ (ready), backoffQ (waiting), unschedulablePods (failed)

### Core Components
- **SchedulingQueue** — Manages pod ordering and state transitions
- **Cache** — In-memory cluster state with assume/forget mechanism  
- **CycleState** — Thread-safe per-pod context for plugin state sharing
- **Framework** — Orchestrates plugins across 14 extension points

The detailed analysis with file references, complete dependency chain, and architectural explanations has been wr
... (truncated)

  "content": "# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis\n\n## Files Examined\n\n### Core Scheduler\n- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** \u2014 Main scheduler struct, initialization, and Run() entry point that starts the scheduling loop\n- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** \u2014 Core scheduling pipeline including ScheduleOne(), schedulingCycle(), bindingCycle(), and schedulePod() methods\n\n### Scheduling Queue & Cache\n- **pkg/scheduler/backend/queue/scheduling_queue.go** \u2014 SchedulingQueue interface with activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods management\n- **pkg/scheduler/backend/cache/cache.go** \u2014 In-memory cluster state cache with assume/forget mechanisms for optimistic binding\n- **pkg/scheduler/backend/cache/snapshot.go** \u2014 Immutable snapshot of cache state used during scheduling\n\n### Plugin Framework\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** \u2014 Framework interfaces and helper types (NodeToStatus, etc.)\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** \u2014 FrameworkImpl that orchestrates plugin execution at all extension points\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** \u2014 CycleState for storing pod-specific state during a scheduling cycle\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go** \u2014 Plugin registry for loading and initializing plugins\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/waiting_pods_map.go** \u2014 Tracking pods waiting in Permit plugin\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/pods_in_prebind_map.go** \u2014 Tracking pods in PreBind phase for preemption\n\n### Supporting Components\n- **pkg/scheduler/profile/** \u2014 Scheduler profiles for multi-scheduler scenarios\n- **pkg/scheduler/backend/api_dispatcher/** \u2014 Async API call dispatcher\n- **pkg/scheduler/backend/workloadmanager/** \u2014 Workload-aware scheduling support\n- **pkg/scheduler/metrics/** \u2014 Metrics collection for scheduler operations\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Entry Point & Initialization\n```\nScheduler.Run() [pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:536]\n  \u2193\n  Starts SchedulingQueue.Run() to accept pods\n  \u2193\n  Spawns goroutine: wait.UntilWithContext(ctx, sched.ScheduleOne, 0)\n```\n\n### 2. Main Scheduling Loop\n```\nScheduler.ScheduleOne() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:66]\n  \u2193\n  Calls NextPod() (which is podQueue.Pop())\n  \u251c\u2500\u2192 Returns next pod from SchedulingQueue\n  \u2514\u2500\u2192 Dispatches to either:\n      \u251c\u2500 scheduleOnePod() [for individual pods]\n      \u2514\u2500 scheduleOnePodGroup() [for workload-aware groups]\n```\n\n### 3. Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous - Find Node)\n```\nscheduleOnePod() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:98]\n  \u2193\n  1. Creates CycleState: framework.NewCycleState()\n  2. Calls schedulingCycle() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:174]\n     \u2193\n     Calls schedulingAlgorithm() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:249]\n     \u2193\n     Calls sched.SchedulePod() \u2192 schedulePod() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:562]\n     \u2193\n     a) updateSnapshot() - Snapshot current cache state\n     \u2193\n     b) findNodesThatFitPod() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:626]\n        \u2193\n        \u2022 RunPreFilterPlugins() [checks pod-level constraints]\n        \u2022 findNodesThatPassFilters() [applies Filter plugins to nodes]\n          \u251c\u2500 parallelized RunFilterPlugins() on candidate nodes\n          \u2514\u2500 applies Extenders for filtering\n        \u2022 findNodesThatPassExtenders() [applies Extender filters]\n        \u2193\n        Returns: feasibleNodes (nodes that passed all filters)\n     \u2193\n     c) prioritizeNodes() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:604]\n        \u2193\n        \u2022 RunPreScorePlugins() [normalize scores]\n        \u2022 parallelized RunScorePlugins() on feasible nodes\n        \u2022 applies Extenders for prioritization\n        \u2193\n        Returns: priorityList (nodes with scores)\n     \u2193\n     d) Selects best node from priorityList\n     \u2193\n     Returns: ScheduleResult with SuggestedHost\n  \u2193\n  3. Calls prepareForBindingCycle() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:197]\n     \u2193\n     a) assumeAndReserve() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:306]\n        \u251c\u2500 assume() [sets NodeName in cache, updates snapshot]\n        \u2514\u2500 RunReservePluginsReserve() [reserve resources]\n     \u2193\n     b) RunPermitPlugins() [blocking admission control]\n        \u2514\u2500 Can approve, wait, or reject scheduling\n```\n\n### 4. Binding Cycle (Asynchronous - Bind to API)\n```\nrunBindingCycle() [async goroutine, pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:150]\n  \u2193\n  bindingCycle() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:390]\n  \u2193\n  1. WaitOnPermit() - Wait for permit plugins if needed\n  \u2193\n  2. RunPreBindPlugins() - Final pre-binding checks\n  \u2193\n  3. bind() - Create actual Pod.Binding to API server\n  \u2193\n  4. RunPostBindPlugins() - Post-binding actions\n  \u2193\n  On failure: unreserveAndForget() - Clean up assumed state\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Architecture Overview\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler uses a **plugin framework** architecture with two clearly separated phases:\n\n#### Phase 1: Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous)\n- **Objective**: Find a suitable node for the pod\n- **Location**: `schedulingCycle()` in `schedule_one.go`\n- **Characteristics**:\n  - Runs to completion synchronously\n  - Works with cluster snapshot (not live state)\n  - May run preemption (PostFilter plugins)\n  - Uses \"assume\" mechanism: pod added to cache **before binding**\n  - Allows next pod to be scheduled while binding is still in progress\n  - Executes serially: only one pod scheduled at a time\n\n#### Phase 2: Binding Cycle (Asynchronous)\n- **Objective**: Persist pod-to-node binding to API server\n- **Location**: `bindingCycle()` in `schedule_one.go`\n- **Characteristics**:\n  - Runs asynchronously in goroutine\n  - Can fail without blocking other scheduling\n  - Includes Permit plugins that can force waiting\n  - If binding fails, RunUnreservePlugins() cleans up resources\n\n### Plugin Framework (Extension Points)\n\nThe framework orchestrates plugins at 14 extension points across the scheduling and binding cycles:\n\n#### Pre-scheduling Phase\n1. **PreEnqueue** \u2014 Filters pods before they enter the queue\n2. **QueueSort** \u2014 Determines pod ordering in the queue\n\n#### Scheduling Cycle Phase\n3. **PreFilter** \u2014 Pod-level checks before filtering nodes\n   - Can filter out nodes at pod level\n   - Results influence which nodes are considered\n4. **Filter** \u2014 Node-level feasibility check (parallelized)\n   - Returns: feasible nodes that satisfy pod requirements\n   - Examples: PodFitsResources, NodeUnschedulable, NoVolumeZoneConflict\n5. **PostFilter** \u2014 Triggered when pod is unschedulable\n   - Handles preemption attempts\n   - Can return nominated node for retry\n6. **PreScore** \u2014 Prepare for scoring phase\n7. **Score** \u2014 Rank feasible nodes (parallelized)\n   - Returns: numeric score for each node\n   - Examples: ImageLocality, InterPodAffinity, TaintToleration\n8. **NormalizeScore** \u2014 Normalize scores from different plugins\n9. **Reserve** \u2014 Resource reservation (first mutating extension point)\n   - Reserves resources in cache\n   - Must be paired with Unreserve for cleanup\n10. **Permit** \u2014 Final admission control, can block/wait\n    - Can approve, reject, or wait for external signal\n    - Last point to reject pod during scheduling\n\n#### Binding Cycle Phase\n11. **PreBind** \u2014 Final pre-binding actions\n    - Examples: volume mounting, network setup\n    - Can still reject pod\n12. **Bind** \u2014 Create actual Pod.Binding to API\n    - Default: DefaultBinder plugin calls API server\n    - Only one BindPlugin can succeed per cycle\n13. **PostBind** \u2014 Post-binding cleanup and logging\n    - Cannot fail or reject\n\n#### Additional\n14. **PreBindPreFlight** \u2014 Preflight checks before PreBind phase\n\n### Plugin Execution Model\n\n**CycleState**: Thread-safe state container (uses sync.Map) for passing data between plugins within a single scheduling cycle:\n- Written once in PreFilter/PreScore phases\n- Read many times in Filter/Score phases\n- Prevents repeated computation\n\n**Parallelization**:\n- Filter plugins run in parallel across nodes (limited by parallelism factor)\n- Score plugins run in parallel across nodes\n- Filter uses a configurable subset of nodes (not all nodes checked)\n- Can evaluate as few as `minFeasibleNodesToFind` (100) nodes\n\n**Plugin Ordering**:\n- Within each extension point, plugins execute in configured order\n- First plugin failure stops the phase (in Filter/PreBind)\n- Score plugins always run to completion, scores are normalized\n\n### Key Data Structures\n\n#### SchedulingQueue (Prioritized Pod Queue)\n```\nSchedulingQueue = activeQ + backoffQ + unschedulablePods\n- activeQ: Pods ready for scheduling (priority ordered)\n- backoffQ: Pods waiting for backoff period (unschedulable retry delay)\n- unschedulablePods: Pods that failed scheduling, only move on cluster events\n```\n\nEvents cause pods to move between queues based on QueueingHints.\n\n#### Cache (Scheduler's View of Cluster)\n```\nCache maintains:\n- assumedPods: Set of pods that have been assumed (scheduled but not bound)\n- podStates: Pod scheduling state\n- nodes: Node information with doubly-linked list (MRU tracking)\n- Snapshot: Immutable view of cache for scheduling\n```\n\nThe **assume** mechanism allows:\n1. Pod added to cache immediately after scheduling decision\n2. NextPod() can get next pod even if previous binding hasn't completed\n3. Binding failure triggers ForgetPod() to revert cache state\n4. This enables high scheduling throughput\n\n#### CycleState\n```\nPer-pod state for one scheduling/binding cycle:\n- storage: sync.Map for thread-safe pod-specific data\n- recordPluginMetrics: Sample plugin metrics\n- skipFilterPlugins: Plugins to skip in Filter phase\n- skipScorePlugins: Plugins to skip in Score phase\n- parallelPreBindPlugins: PreBind plugins that can run in parallel\n```\n\n### Complete Flow Example\n\n```\nUser creates Pod\n  \u2193\nEvent handler adds Pod to SchedulingQueue (activeQ)\n  \u2193\nScheduler.ScheduleOne() pops pod\n  \u2193\nSCHEDULING CYCLE (synchronous):\n  1. CreateSnapshot from cache\n  2. RunPreFilterPlugins(pod) \u2192 get node candidates\n  3. For each candidate node in parallel:\n     - RunFilterPlugins(pod, node) \u2192 feasible nodes\n  4. If no feasible nodes:\n     - RunPostFilterPlugins(pod) \u2192 attempt preemption\n       \u2514\u2500 May return nominated node\n  5. For each feasible node in parallel:\n     - RunScorePlugins(pod, node) \u2192 scores\n  6. Select highest-scored node\n  7. RunReservePlugins(pod, node) \u2192 reserve resources in cache\n  8. assume(pod, node) \u2192 update snapshot with NodeName set\n  9. RunPermitPlugins(pod, node) \u2192 can wait/reject\n  \u2193\n  If scheduling succeeded, launch async goroutine:\n  \u2193\nBINDING CYCLE (asynchronous):\n  1. WaitOnPermit(pod) \u2192 wait for permit plugins\n  2. RunPreBindPlugins(pod, node) \u2192 final checks\n  3. Call Bind plugin:\n     - DefaultBinder creates Pod.Binding in API server\n  4. RunPostBindPlugins(pod, node) \u2192 logging/cleanup\n  \u2193\nBinding succeeds \u2192 Pod scheduled\nBinding fails \u2192 RunUnreservePlugins() \u2192 ForgetPod() \u2192 Pod back to queue\n```\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n1. **Two-Phase Scheduling**: Separate find (sync) and bind (async) phases enable concurrent scheduling\n\n2. **Assume Pattern**: Optimistically assume binding will succeed, use snapshot isolation to avoid conflicts\n\n3. **Plugin Registry**: All scheduling logic pluggable via framework interface (no hardcoded algorithm)\n\n4. **Extension Points**: Strategic points throughout pipeline where plugins can be injected\n\n5. **Snapshot Isolation**: Work with immutable snapshots to avoid race conditions while async binding occurs\n\n6. **Parallelization**: Filter and Score phases parallelized across nodes to handle large clusters\n\n7. **Queueing Hints**: Plugins provide hints about which cluster events should requeue specific pods\n\n8. **Preemption Support**: PostFilter plugins attempt preemption when pod is unschedulable\n\n### Configuration & Profiles\n\n- **Multiple Profiles**: Different schedulers can run with different configurations\n- **Extenders**: Legacy support for out-of-tree filtering/prioritizing\n- **Feature Gates**: Enable/disable features like SchedulerAsyncAPICalls, GenericWorkload, OpportunisticBatching\n\n### Concurrency & Performance\n\n- **Parallelism**: Filter and Score plugins use configurable thread pool\n- **Percentage of Nodes to Score**: Optimization to evaluate only a percentage of feasible nodes\n- **Metrics Sampling**: Only sample plugin metrics on ~10% of cycles to reduce overhead\n- **Async Binding**: Binding happens asynchronously so scheduler doesn't wait for API responses\n- **Async API Calls**: Optional APIDispatcher for batched/async API calls (SchedulerAsyncAPICalls feature)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated plugin framework with a **two-phase design**: a synchronous scheduling cycle that finds a suitable node using a series of filtering and scoring plugins, followed by an asynchronous binding cycle that persists the decision to the API server. The \"assume\" mechanism enables concurrent scheduling by optimistically updating an in-memory cache before binding completes, allowing the next pod to be scheduled while binding is still in progress. The plugin framework with 14 extension points enables full customization of scheduling behavior without modifying core scheduler code, while parallelization of filter and score plugins enables scalability to large clusters.\n",

Returns: numeric score for each node\n   - Examples: ImageLocality, InterPodAffinity, TaintToleration\n8. **NormalizeScore** \u2014 Normalize scores from different plugins\n9. **Reserve** \u2014 Resource reservation (first mutating extension point)\n   - Reserves resources in cache\n   - Must be paired with Unreserve for cleanup\n10. **Permit** \u2014 Final admission control, can block/wait\n    - Can approve, reject, or wait for external signal\n    - Last point to reject pod during scheduling\n\n#### Binding Cycle Phase\n11. **PreBind** \u2014 Final pre-binding actions\n    - Examples: volume mounting, network setup\n    - Can still reject pod\n12. **Bind** \u2014 Create actual Pod.Binding to API\n    - Default: DefaultBinder plugin calls API server\n    - Only one BindPlugin can succeed per cycle\n13. **PostBind** \u2014 Post-binding cleanup and logging\n    - Cannot fail or reject\n\n#### Additional\n14. **PreBindPreFlight** \u2014 Preflight checks before PreBind phase\n\n### Plugin Execution Model\n\n**CycleState**: Thread-safe state container (uses sync.Map) for passing data between plugins within a single scheduling cycle:\n- Written once in PreFilter/PreScore phases\n- Read many times in Filter/Score phases\n- Prevents repeated computation\n\n**Parallelization**:\n- Filter plugins run in parallel across nodes (limited by parallelism factor)\n- Score plugins run in parallel across nodes\n- Filter uses a configurable subset of nodes (not all nodes checked)\n- Can evaluate as few as `minFeasibleNodesToFind` (100) nodes\n\n**Plugin Ordering**:\n- Within each extension point, plugins execute in configured order\n- First plugin failure stops the phase (in Filter/PreBind)\n- Score plugins always run to completion, scores are normalized\n\n### Key Data Structures\n\n#### SchedulingQueue (Prioritized Pod Queue)\n```\nSchedulingQueue = activeQ + backoffQ + unschedulablePods\n- activeQ: Pods ready for scheduling (priority ordered)\n- backoffQ: Pods waiting for backoff period (unschedulable retry delay)\n- unschedulablePods: Pods that failed scheduling, only move on cluster events\n```\n\nEvents cause pods to move between queues based on QueueingHints.\n\n#### Cache (Scheduler's View of Cluster)\n```\nCache maintains:\n- assumedPods: Set of pods that have been assumed (scheduled but not bound)\n- podStates: Pod scheduling state\n- nodes: Node information with doubly-linked list (MRU tracking)\n- Snapshot: Immutable view of cache for scheduling\n```\n\nThe **assume** mechanism allows:\n1. Pod added to cache immediately after scheduling decision\n2. NextPod() can get next pod even if previous binding hasn't completed\n3. Binding failure triggers ForgetPod() to revert cache state\n4. This enables high scheduling throughput\n\n#### CycleState\n```\nPer-pod state for one scheduling/binding cycle:\n- storage: sync.Map for thread-safe pod-specific data\n- recordPluginMetrics: Sample plugin metrics\n- skipFilterPlugins: Plugins to skip in Filter phase\n- skipScorePlugins: Plugins to skip in Score phase\n- parallelPreBindPlugins: PreBind plugins that can run in parallel\n```\n\n### Complete Flow Example\n\n```\nUser creates Pod\n  \u2193\nEvent handler adds Pod to SchedulingQueue (activeQ)\n  \u2193\nScheduler.ScheduleOne() pops pod\n  \u2193\nSCHEDULING CYCLE (synchronous):\n  1. CreateSnapshot from cache\n  2. RunPreFilterPlugins(pod) \u2192 get node candidates\n  3. For each candidate node in parallel:\n     - RunFilterPlugins(pod, node) \u2192 feasible nodes\n  4. If no feasible nodes:\n     - RunPostFilterPlugins(pod) \u2192 attempt preemption\n       \u2514\u2500 May return nominated node\n  5. For each feasible node in parallel:\n     - RunScorePlugins(pod, node) \u2192 scores\n  6. Select highest-scored node\n  7. RunReservePlugins(pod, node) \u2192 reserve resources in cache\n  8. assume(pod, node) \u2192 update snapshot with NodeName set\n  9. RunPermitPlugins(pod, node) \u2192 can wait/reject\n  \u2193\n  If scheduling succeeded, launch async goroutine:\n  \u2193\nBINDING CYCLE (asynchronous):\n  1. WaitOnPermit(pod) \u2192 wait for permit plugins\n  2. RunPreBindPlugins(pod, node) \u2192 final checks\n  3. Call Bind plugin:\n     - DefaultBinder creates Pod.Binding in API server\n  4. RunPostBindPlugins(pod, node) \u2192 logging/cleanup\n  \u2193\nBinding succeeds \u2192 Pod scheduled\nBinding fails \u2192 RunUnreservePlugins() \u2192 ForgetPod() \u2192 Pod back to queue\n```\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n1. **Two-Phase Scheduling**: Separate find (sync) and bind (async) phases enable concurrent scheduling\n\n2. **Assume Pattern**: Optimistically assume binding will succeed, use snapshot isolation to avoid conflicts\n\n3. **Plugin Registry**: All scheduling logic pluggable via framework interface (no hardcoded algorithm)\n\n4. **Extension Points**: Strategic points throughout pipeline where plugins can be injected\n\n5. **Snapshot Isolation**: Work with immutable snapshots to avoid race conditions while async binding occurs\n\n6. **Parallelization**: Filter and Score phases parallelized across nodes to handle large clusters\n\n7. **Queueing Hints**: Plugins provide hints about which cluster events should requeue specific pods\n\n8. **Preemption Support**: PostFilter plugins attempt preemption when pod is unschedulable\n\n### Configuration & Profiles\n\n- **Multiple Profiles**: Different schedulers can run with different configurations\n- **Extenders**: Legacy support for out-of-tree filtering/prioritizing\n- **Feature Gates**: Enable/disable features like SchedulerAsyncAPICalls, GenericWorkload, OpportunisticBatching\n\n### Concurrency & Performance\n\n- **Parallelism**: Filter and Score plugins use configurable thread pool\n- **Percentage of Nodes to Score**: Optimization to evaluate only a percentage of feasible nodes\n- **Metrics Sampling**: Only sample plugin metrics on ~10% of cycles to reduce overhead\n- **Async Binding**: Binding happens asynchronously so scheduler doesn't wait for API responses\n- **Async API Calls**: Optional APIDispatcher for batched/async API calls (SchedulerAsyncAPICalls feature)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated plugin framework with a **two-phase design**: a synchronous scheduling cycle that finds a suitable node using a series of filtering and scoring plugins, followed by an asynchronous binding cycle that persists the decision to the API server. The \"assume\" mechanism enables concurrent scheduling by optimistically updating an in-memory cache before binding completes, allowing the next pod to be scheduled while binding is still in progress. The plugin framework with 14 extension points enables full customization of scheduling behavior without modifying core scheduler code, while parallelization of filter and score plugins enables scalability to large clusters.\n",
  "filePath": "/logs/agent/solution.md",
  "originalFile": null,
  "structuredPatch": [],
  "type": "create"

1. WRITE /logs/agent/solution.md
# Kubernetes Scheduler Architecture Analysis

## Files Examined

### Core Scheduler
- **pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go** — Main scheduler struct, initialization, and Run() entry point that starts the scheduling loop
- **pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go** — Core scheduling pipeline including ScheduleOne(), schedulingCycle(), bindingCycle(), and schedulePod() methods

### Scheduling Queue & Cache
- **pkg/scheduler/backend/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — SchedulingQueue interface with activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods management
- **pkg/scheduler/backend/cache/cache.go** — In-memory cluster state cache with assume/forget mechanisms for optimistic binding
- **pkg/scheduler/backend/cache/snapshot.go** — Immutable snapshot of cache state used during scheduling

### Plugin Framework
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go** — Framework interfaces and helper types (NodeToStatus, etc.)
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go** — FrameworkImpl that orchestrates plugin execution at all extension points
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/cycle_state.go** — CycleState for storing pod-specific state during a scheduling cycle
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go** — Plugin registry for loading and initializing plugins
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/waiting_pods_map.go** — Tracking pods waiting in Permit plugin
- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/pods_in_prebind_map.go** — Tracking pods in PreBind phase for preemption

### Supporting Components
- **pkg/scheduler/profile/** — Scheduler profiles for multi-scheduler scenarios
- **pkg/scheduler/backend/api_dispatcher/** — Async API call dispatcher
- **pkg/scheduler/backend/workloadmanager/** — Workload-aware scheduling support
- **pkg/scheduler/metrics/** — Metrics collection for scheduler operations

## Dependency Chain
